# 1\. Introduction

Razorpay APIs return either a success or failure response. While the guidelines for designing the API have been detailed in the ​​[API Design Guide](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/edit?usp=sharing), many product and engineering folks still struggle with creating good error responses. The document's objective is to provide clear directions on creating well-defined error responses, outline the key components involved, and present the approach to be followed when designing an error response to ensure consistency and accuracy across systems.  
Note: The audience is expected to be familiar with [API Design Guide](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/edit?usp=sharing), and this document will not repeat the concepts discussed there.

# 2\. What are error responses?

An error response from an API from Razorpay signals that something went wrong with a request. Instead of returning the expected data, the API sends back an error response containing information about the problem encountered. The JSON error response is returned with the relevant error parameters, which allows developers and businesses to track and analyze the most common reasons for failures in their systems.  
Error responses provide valuable information that can be used to:

* Pinpoint the failure source: They help identify whether the problem originates from the user, the API provider (Razorpay), a payment gateway, a bank, or the network.  
* Identify the specific step that resulted in failure: They highlight the stage of the transaction where the failure occurred (e.g. payment authentication, payment authorization).  
* Guide user actions: They provide the opportunity to present users with clear messages and guidance on appropriate next steps to resolve the issue.  
* Analyze failure reasons: The response will have details that can help you drill down and correct the error without having to refer to other documentation.

Well-handled errors lead to a better user experience. Instead of encountering confusing technical messages, users receive clear explanations and guidance on resolving issues and developers can avoid time-consuming debugging sessions. Logs generated from error responses can be further analyzed to identify trends and potential areas for improvement.

# 3\. What are the components of an error response?

The standard Razorpay error response is in the following format.

| { "error": {   "code": "\<ERROR\_TYPE\>",   "internal\_error\_code": "\<ERROR\_TYPE\>", //internal   "description": "\<DESCRIPTION\>",   "source": "\<SOURCE\>",   "step": "\<STEP\>",   "reason": "\<REASON\>",     "field": "\<FIELD\>",   "next\_best\_action": "\<NEXT\_BEST\_ACTION\>", //internal     "failure\_type": "\<FAILURE\_TYPE\>", //internal     "merchant\_desc": "\<MERCHANT\_DESCRIPTION\>",//internal     "money\_implication": "\<MONEY\_IMPLICATION\>",//internal     "perception": "\<PERCEPTION\>",//internal     "rzp\_actionable": "\<RAZORPAY\_ACTIONABLE\>",//internal   "metadata": {     "payment\_id": "\<PAYMENT\_ID\>",     "order\_id": "\<ORDER\_ID\>",     "gateway": {       "method\_error\_code": "\<METHOD\_ERROR\_CODE\>",    }   } }} |
| :---- |

The key components of the above message are detailed below.

| Field | Internal/ Public | Datatype | Mandatory / Optional | Comments |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| code | Public | string | Mandatory | Code is a string that represents a high-level categorization of an error. The field can have the following 3 possible values. BAD\_REQUEST\_ERROR SERVER\_ERROR GATEWAY ERROR |
| description | Public | string | Mandatory | Text detailing the nature of the error |
| source | Public | string | Mandatory | Point of failure in this specific operation. |
| step | Public | string | Mandatory | The stage where the failure occurred. |
| reason | Public | string | Mandatory | The exact reason for the failure |
| field | Public | string | Optional | The field that caused the failure |
| internal\_error\_code | Internal | string | Mandatory | Type of error \- to be used internally and not to be exposed to merchant |
| next\_best\_action | Internal | string | Optional | Possible next best action |
| failure\_type | Internal | String | Optional | Type of failure. Possible values are 1\) Business 2\) Technical |
| merchant\_desc | Internal | String | Optional | A description of the reason for failure is to be shown on the merchant/admin dashboard. |
| money\_implication | Internal | String | Optional | A description of what happens to the money due to the failure in servicing the request should be shown on the merchant/admin dashboard. |
| perception | Internal | String | Optional | Description to be shown on merchant/admin dashboard on general perception about the failure |
| rzp\_actionable | Internal | String | Optional | The field determines whether to trigger an automated response to a merchant or not. Possible values are “NoAction” and “CreateAutoResponse” |
| next\_step | Internal | String | Optional | The next step to be taken by the merchant will be described on the merchant/admin dashboard. |
| metadata | Public | Object | Optional | The object will share additional details to debug the error, including payment and order ID, gateway error details, etc. Refer to section 3.6. Metadata for more details, including metadata gateway fields. |

## 3.1. Code

Code is a string that represents a high-level categorization of an error. The field can have the following 3 possible values.

### 3.1.1. Bad Request Error

A Bad Request Error (HTTP Status Code 400\) occurs when a server cannot process the request sent by the client due to client-side errors. This error indicates that the request is malformed or invalid.  
Razorpay will return a Bad Request Error when

* The issue is occurring due to a client-side error or  
* Razorpay send this to a third party (say Bank) and the third party informs us that there is an error in input data

| { "error": {   "code": "BAD\_REQUEST\_ERROR",   "description": "Authentication failed due to incorrect otp",   "source": "customer",   "step": "payment\_authentication",   "reason": "invalid\_otp",   "metadata": {     "payment\_id": "pay\_EDNBKIP31Y4jl8",     "order\_id": "order\_DBJKIP31Y4jl8"   } }} |
| :---- |

### 3.1.2. Server Error

A Server Error (HTTP Status Code 500\) occurs when the server encounters an unexpected condition that prevents it from fulfilling the client's request. This is a generic error message indicating that something has gone wrong on the server's side.

| { "error": {   "code" : "SERVER\_ERROR",   "description" : "Your payment could not be completed due to a temporary technical issue. To complete the payment, use another payment method.",   "source": "internal",   "step": "payment\_initiation",   "reason": "server\_error",   "field": "null",   "metadata": {     "payment\_id": "pay\_EDNBKIP31Y4jl8",     "order\_id": "order\_DBJKIP31Y4jl8"   } }} |
| :---- |

### 3.1.3. Gateway Errors

A gateway error indicates a technical issue with the gateway. For Gateway errors, the error response is populated based on the fields provided by the payment gateways, wallets, NPCI etc depending on the method.

| { "error": {   "code" : "GATEWAY\_ERROR",   "description" : "Payment processing failed due to error at bank or wallet gateway",   "source": "issuer\_bank",   "step": "payment\_authorization",   "reason": "card\_declined",   "field": "null",   "next\_best\_action": "System Retry",   "metadata": {     "payment\_id": "pay\_EDNBKIP31Y4jl8",     "order\_id": "order\_DBJKIP31Y4jl8"   } }} |
| :---- |

Gateway errors can have additional data in the metadata field which could help developers debug the issue further. More on that in section [3.6. Metadata](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#h.ygm6fqcnykdy)

## 3.2. Description

The “description” field should contain a clear, human-readable explanation of what went wrong. For example, "Authentication failed due to incorrect otp" effectively conveys the reason for the error. Developers integrating the API will then be able to capture the error description and directly show the content to the end-user.  
**Formatting content**: The description should follow standard formatting for content displayed in the merchant UI. Start with a capital letter, avoid special characters and acronyms, and keep the content restricted to a maximum of two sentences and under 255 characters.  
**Target Audience**: End users who initiate a transaction and developers are potential candidates for receiving the information shared in the “description” field. Hence someone without a deep technical understanding should be able to decipher the information and understand what went wrong with a given transaction from the information shared in this field.  
**Conciseness with clarity**: A sniff test to check if the error description is adequate is to ask

* Can the merchant display the information in the description field directly in their UI?  
* Will the end user be able to understand the reason for failure from the content shared in this field?

**Avoid sensitive information**: Error descriptions should not include sensitive information like passwords or internal system details.

## 3.3. Source

The ‘source’ field points to the cause of failure. It provides valuable information on which entity in the process is responsible for the error. The values for the ‘source’ field are restricted and are listed below.

| Source | Description |
| :---- | :---- |
| customer | The error was caused by the customer, such as entering an incorrect OTP or exceeding transaction limits. |
| business | The error originated in the merchant system and was caused by something the merchant did, such as sending an invalid API request. |
| internal | The source is within Razorpay; the error was caused by something on Razorpay's end, not by the merchant or customer. |
| gateway | The error originated from the gateway, the service that connects Razorpay to the banks and other financial institutions. |
| issuer\_bank | The source of error is the issuing bank |
| network | The error occurred at the network level, such as the UPI network or the card network |
| beneficiary\_bank | The source of error is the beneficiary bank which will be receiving the payment |
| issuer | The source of error is the issuing bank/agency |

**Target Audience**: The data in the ‘source’ field is intended primarily for developers to identify the source of failure and take appropriate corrective action. The field should be programmatically readable, and when adding a new source, it should follow the underscore format (e.g., "beneficiary\_bank"). Additionally, the merchant's analytics team can use this information to track error trends and identify any recurring issues.  
Please read through section 3.4. Step for further details on how the source field can be arrived at for a given transaction.

## 3.4. Step

The ‘step’ field indicates the stage in the process where the error occurred. The ‘source’ and ‘step’ fields can have different values depending on the transaction processing method used. Having the correct ‘step’ information is critical, especially in multi-step operations like payments, where understanding a specific failure step is required for troubleshooting an issue. The exhaustive list of ‘step’ can be viewed in the doc[Error Mapping Module](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1kZR2WOFCMlcwa6PILuVnyBMhnAnxXsOD4j_BmnFGujQ/edit?usp=sharing).  
**Target audience**: The step field is intended for developers debugging the issue or analytics teams evaluating the trend. The data in the field should be programmatically accessible. Given that the values for ‘step’ are expected to be accessed programmatically, it is suggested to use underscore as in “payment\_authorization”.  
**Clarity and comprehensiveness**: Avoid using abbreviations or technical jargon while creating a step field, as this will confuse the developer. Identifying the correct step fields requires a good understanding of the entire process for a given method, as outlined in section [3.4.1. Cards](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#h.78csh2bhjj3d), [3.4.2. UPI](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#h.z4u0h1rvwvxw), [3.4.3. Netbanking](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#h.5scgset7r6lc), [3.4.4. Wallet](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#h.scs7yd25s78), [3.4.5. Cardless EMI](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#h.y6ax26u2aqwv), [3.4.6. Emandate](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#h.nq2hqrmjch2c).  
Let's take a look at why source and step are important with the below example.

| { "error": {   "code" : "GATEWAY\_ERROR",   "description" : "Payment processing failed due to error at bank or wallet gateway",   "source": "issuer\_bank",   "step": "payment\_authorization",   "reason": "card\_declined",   "metadata": {     "payment\_id": "pay\_EDNBKIP31Y4jl8",     "order\_id": "order\_DBJKIP31Y4jl8"   } }} |
| :---- |

In the above example, a developer reading the code and description should understand that this is an error with the bank. However, without a source, it will be difficult for the developer to pinpoint the source of the error—which in this case is the ‘issuer\_bank’. Further, the ‘step’ gives details of the stage in which the error occurred, giving a complete picture of the origin and path.  
**Note:** The step field can have a ‘null’ value in some cases. For example, in a case where an API cannot be fired (details [here](https://razorpay.com/docs/errors/x/#api-error-codes)), there is no step involved, and the field value will be ‘null’.  
In a payment flow, the parameters for source and step are restricted based on the methods. The following sections for individual methods outline the possible values for source and step.

### 3.4.1. Cards

The payment flow for Card payments is illustrated below.  
![Errors Payment Methods Cards][image1]  
The possible values for the step parameter, along with the description, are listed below:

* payment\_initiation: The merchant system initiates and sends the payment request to our server. Our server validates your request, creates the payment flow and forwards the request to the Gateway.  
* card\_enrollment\_check: Upon receiving a request from Razorpay, Gateway sends the enrollment check request to the bank for the enrollment of the card check.  
* payment\_authentication: The bank verifies the enrollment of the card, and then requests the authentication of the customer by sending a 3DS URL and OTP to the customer.  
* 3DS URL: Bank sends the Authentication (3DS URL), which is routed through Gateway \> Razorpay \> Customer.  
* OTP: The bank sends the OTP directly to the customer’s mobile. The customer enters the valid OTP within the time limit on the bank's OTP page.  
* payment\_authorization: Once the customer has completed the authentication, the bank authorizes the release of the funds. The authorisation status is communicated to the Gateway, which in turn communicates it to Razorpay.  
* payment\_capture: Once the payment is successfully authorized, Razorpay sends the capture request to the Gateway, which in turn sends it to the bank to capture the authorized payment.

### **3.4.2. UPI**

**UPI** payments can further be bifurcated to intent and collect flows.

#### Intent Flow

The payment flow for UPI Intent payments is illustrated below.  
![][image2]  
The possible values for the step parameter for UPI Intent flow, along with the description, are listed below:

* mandate\_creation: Request to create a new UPI mandate.  
* payment\_initiation: The merchant system initiates and sends the payment request to our server.  
* payment\_creation: Razorpay creates an intent URL and passes it back to you.  
* payment\_authentication: The payer clicks on the pay button (pointing to the intent URL), which prompts the payer to open the PSP App. After the App opens, the payer enters the M-PIN on the PSP App, and then authenticates the transaction.  
* payment\_request: Payer PSP sends the payment request to the UPI network.  
* payment\_request\_beneficiary\_details: The UPI network requests the beneficiary details from the Payee PSP.  
* payment\_response\_beneficiary\_details: Payee PSP sends the beneficiary details to the UPI network.  
* payment\_debit\_request: The UPI network requests a debit of the given payment amount from the customer's bank.  
* payment\_debit\_response: The customer’s bank sends the debit response to the NPCI.  
* payment\_credit\_request: The UPI network sends the payment credit request to your account maintained with Razorpay.  
* payment\_credit\_response: The beneficiary bank sends the credit response to the UPI network.  
* payment\_status\_request: The UPI network requests the transaction confirmation status from Payee PSP which acts as the gateway in UPI transactions.  
* payment\_status\_response: Payee PSP sends the transaction confirmation response to the UPI Network.  
* payment\_response: Payee PSP sends the callback to our server. This will contain the final transaction status.  
* refund\_request: Request to initiate a refund.

#### Collect Flow

The payment flow for UPI Collect payments is illustrated below.  
![][image3]  
The possible values for the step parameter for the UPI Collect flow, along with the description, are listed below:

* mandate\_creation: Request to create a new UPI mandate.  
* payment\_initiation: The merchant system initiates and sends the payment request to our server.  
* payment\_creation: Razorpay creates the payment and sends the collect request via Payee PSP (Gateway).  
* payment\_request: Payee PSP sends the payment request to the UPI network.  
* payment\_authentication\_request: The UPI network sends an authentication request for the given payment amount to the Payer PSP.  
* payment\_authentication: The customer clicks on the payment notification received on mobile which opens the PSP App. After the App opens, the customer enters the M-PIN on the PSP App, and then authenticates the transaction.  
* payment\_authentication\_response: Payer PSP sends the authentication details to the UPI network.  
* payment\_debit\_request: Upon successful authentication, the UPI network requests a debit of the given payment amount from the customer's bank.  
* payment\_debit\_response: Customer’s bank sends the debit response to the UPI Network.  
* payment\_credit\_request: The UPI network sends the payment credit request to your account maintained with Razorpay.  
* payment\_credit\_response: The beneficiary bank sends the credit response to the UPI network.  
* payment\_status\_request: UPI network sends the transaction confirmation request to payer PSP (Google Pay).  
* payment\_status\_response: Payer PSP (Google Pay) sends acknowledge, informs the customer and sends the response to NPCI.  
* payment\_response: Payee PSP sends the callback to our server. This will contain the final transaction status.  
* refund\_request: Request to initiate a refund.

### 3.4.3. Netbanking

The payment flow for Netbanking payments is illustrated below:  
![Errors Payment Methods Netbanking][image4]  
The possible values for the step parameter, along with the description, are listed below:

* payment\_initiation: The merchant system initiates and sends the payment request to our server. Razorpay then sends the bank URL back to you.  
* payment\_authentication: The customer logs into his netbanking account and completes the transaction.  
* payment\_authorization: Upon successful authentication, the bank authorizes the release of funds and notifies Razorpay, which in turn notifies the business.

### 3.4.4. Wallet

The payment flow for Wallet payments is illustrated below:  
![Errors Payment Methods Wallets][image5]  
The possible values for the step parameter, along with the description, are listed below:

* payment\_initiation: The merchant system initiates and sends the payment request to our server. Our server sends the same request to the Bank/Gateway.  
* payment\_eligibility\_check: Razorpay sends the eligibility check request to the issuer to determine if the entered customer information is correct.  
* payment\_authentication: Customer authenticates the payment using OTP provided by the issuer.  
* payment\_authorization: Issuer authorizes the release of funds and sends a confirmation to Razorpay.

### 3.4.5. Cardless EMI

The payment flow for **Cardless EMI** payments is illustrated below:  
![Errors Payment Methods Cardless EMI][image6]  
The possible values for the step parameter, along with the description, are listed below:

* payment\_initiation: The merchant system initiates and sends the payment request to our server. Our server sends the same request to the Bank/Gateway.  
* payment\_eligibility\_check: Razorpay sends the eligibility check request to the issuer to determine if the entered customer information is correct and to determine the credit eligibility of the customer.  
* payment\_authentication: Customer authenticates the payment using OTP provided by the issuer.  
* payment\_authorization: The Issuer authorizes the release of funds and sends a confirmation to Razorpay.

### 3.4.6. Emandate

The possible values for the step parameter, along with the description, are listed below:

* payment\_initiation: The merchant system initiates and sends the payment request to our server. Our server validates your request, creates the payment flow, and forwards the request to the Gateway.  
* payment\_authentication: The bank verifies the enrollment of the Emandate by asking customers to authenticate themselves.  
* payment\_authorization: Once the customer has completed the authentication, the bank authorizes the release of the funds. The authorization status is communicated to the Gateway, which in turn communicates it to Razorpay.

## 3.4. Reason

The reason field pinpoints the exact reason for failure and is meant to be an actionable explanation for why the request failed. In conjunction with the source and step, the field can be used by developers to trigger specific actions or business logic within their applications. The exhaustive set of reasons for a given ‘source’, ‘step’ and ‘method’ can be viewed in [Error Mapping Module](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1kZR2WOFCMlcwa6PILuVnyBMhnAnxXsOD4j_BmnFGujQ/edit?usp=sharing).  
**Target audience**: The field is intended for developers and analytics teams and is expected to be machine-readable. Hence, it is suggested to use underscore as in “insufficient\_funds”. The field is not expected to be descriptive.  
**Actionability**: A developer integrating the API will depend on getting accurate information from this field to design precise error-handling workflows. Hence, the value of the reason field should be designed to share an accurate and actionable reason.  
**Reason vs Description**: The "reason" field is designed to be machine-readable and helps identify the specific error. It's intended to assist developers in categorizing and troubleshooting the issue.  
The "description" field, on the other hand, contains a more detailed explanation that can be understood by both developers and end users. It provides context for the failure, making it easier to understand what went wrong.  
 

| { "error": {   "code" : "GATEWAY\_ERROR",   "description" : "Payment processing failed due to error at bank or wallet gateway",   "source": "issuer\_bank",   "step": "payment\_authorization",   "reason": "card\_declined",   "field": "null",   "next\_best\_action": "System Retry",   "metadata": {     "payment\_id": "pay\_EDNBKIP31Y4jl8",     "order\_id": "order\_DBJKIP31Y4jl8"   } }} |
| :---- |

## 3.5. Field

The field parameter in Razorpay API helps to identify the specific parameter in the API request that caused the error. Identifying the problematic field will help developers to diagnose the issue faster and identify the root cause.  
**Target audience**: The field is intended for developers to pinpoint the field that is responsible for the error.

| { "error": {   "code" : "BAD\_REQUEST\_ERROR",   "internal\_error\_code": "BAD\_REQUEST\_PAYMENT\_INVALID\_AMOUNT",   "description": "Amount is mandatory",   "source": "business",   "step": "payment\_initiation",   "reason": "invalid\_amount",   "field": "amount", }} |
| :---- |

In the above example, ‘field’ clearly specifies that the failure was caused by the ‘amount’ parameter. The error is relevant for ‘BAD\_REQUEST\_ERROR’ and will be empty/null in other cases.

## 3.6. Metadata

The metadata provides supplementary information that will help to further debug the issue. The entity is expected to have an order ID and payment ID wherever applicable. Additionally, It can contain gateway-specific information within the gateway object.  
**Target Audience**: The metadata content is expected to explain the error in detail. The entity is intended for developers who want to deep-dive and find further information on the reason and path of the error.  

| { "error": {   "code" : "BAD\_REQUEST\_ERROR",   "internal\_error\_code": "BAD\_REQUEST\_PAYMENT\_INVALID\_AMOUNT",   "description": "Amount is mandatory",   "source": "business",   "step": "payment\_initiation",   "reason": "invalid\_amount",   "field": "amount",   "metadata": {     "payment\_id": "pay\_EDNBKIP31Y4jl8",     "order\_id": "order\_DBJKIP31Y4jl8"   } }} |
| :---- |

*Note: Gateway errors received are exposed to specific merchants using a feature flag. Details can be viewed here* [GatewayErrorCodes](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Nkha5HRBvbly8ueR269M5cqwdx53e0ds1tNUuyEVxDw/edit?tab=t.0)*. This is not a common practice and is done on a need to have basis.*

### 3.6.1. UPI Switch

For UPI Switch gateway errors, the error response is populated based on the fields provided by NPCI.  
The gateway fields, which are part of metadata, include

* upi\_error\_code  
* upi\_payer\_resp\_code  
* upi\_payee\_resp\_code  
* upi\_payer\_reversal\_resp\_code  
* Upi\_payee\_reversal\_resp\_code

| { "error": {   "code": "GATEWAY\_ERROR",   "description" : "Payment was unsuccessful as the receiver's bank account is inactive. Any amount deducted will be refunded within 5-7 working days.",   "source": "beneficiary\_bank",   "step": "payment\_credit\_request",   "reason": "beneficiary\_account\_dormant",   "field": null   "metadata": {       "payment\_id": "pay\_EDNBKIP31Y4jl8",     "order\_id": "order\_DBJKIP31Y4jl8"     "gateway": {       "upi\_error\_code": "U31",       "payer\_resp\_code": "00",       "upi\_payee\_resp\_code": "ZY",       "payer\_reversal\_resp\_code": "",       "payee\_reversal\_resp\_code": ""     }   } }} |
| :---- |

## 3.7. internal\_error\_code (Internal)

The internal error code, as the name describes, is internal to the system and is not intended to be shared in merchant-facing documentation. This field serves the following purpose

* Uniquely identify and map a given error content. For example, different gateways can respond with errors of a similar nature. These external messages can be mapped to a unique internal error code, thereby ensuring consistency in merchant-facing messages.  
* Avoid duplication: Internal error code helps to map different external errors to a unique internal error message

| { "error": {   "code" : "BAD\_REQUEST\_ERROR",   "description": "Account Balance is insufficient",   "internal\_error\_code": "BAD\_REQUEST\_PAYMENT\_ACCOUNT\_INSUFFICIENT\_BALANCE"   "source": "customer",   "step": "payment\_authorization",   "reason": "insufficient\_funds",   "next\_best\_action": "Insufficient balance \- Retry with another card or payment method",   "field": null,   "metadata": {     "payment\_id": "pay\_EDNBKIP31Y4jl8",     "order\_id": "order\_DBJKIP31Y4jl8"   } }} |
| :---- |

## 3.8. next\_best\_action (Internal)

This field aims to guide merchants towards the most suitable course of action based on the specific error encountered. The field is not currently exposed to merchants. However, while designing the error message, it is suggested that the content of the field be populated wherever applicable for future use.

| { "error": {   "code" : "BAD\_REQUEST\_ERROR",   "description": "Account Balance is insufficient",   "source": "customer",   "step": "payment\_authorization",   "reason": "insufficient\_funds",   "next\_best\_action": "Insufficient balance \- Retry with another card or payment method",   "field": null,   "metadata": {     "payment\_id": "pay\_EDNBKIP31Y4jl8",     "order\_id": "order\_DBJKIP31Y4jl8"   } }} |
| :---- |

## 3.9. failure\_type (Internal)

The ‘failure\_type’ field is used to classify the error reason for further analysis. The field can take two possible values:

* Business: The error occurs when the request fails due to an issue with a business functionality logic or a user workflow. For e.g. if a user enters an incorrect or expired OTP, then the failure is due to how the user interacts with the system and is classified as ‘Business’  
* Technical: This type of error occurs when the request fails due to a system, network, or server issue. For instance, a ‘payment\_timeout’ is a technical error, as the system was not able to complete processing the request.

| { "error": {   "code" : "BAD\_REQUEST\_ERROR",   "description": "Payment processing failed because of expired OTP.",   "source": "customer",   "step": "payment\_authentication",   "reason": "otp\_expired",   "failure\_type": "Business",   "metadata": {     "payment\_id": "pay\_EDNBKIP31Y4jl8",     "order\_id": "order\_DBJKIP31Y4jl8"   } }} |
| :---- |

## 3.10. merchant\_desc (Internal)

This field provides a concise description of the reason for the error, tailored for display on the merchant or admin dashboard.  
**Content and Formatting**: Given that the field needs to be displayed in the dashboard UI, ensure to have a brief description of the error scenario not exceeding two sentences. The content can have information relevant to the error from a business perspective. For example, if the payment timed out, the description could be "The payment couldn't be completed as the customer exceeded the time limit for payment processing. This time limit is typically 10 mins unless otherwise specified."

## 3.11. money\_implication (Internal)

This field explains the financial consequences of the error for the merchant, specifically addressing what happens to the funds involved. The content of the field is intended for the admin and merchant dashboards.  
**Content and Formatting**: The description should clearly state ‘What will happen to the money deducted?’ from a merchant’s perspective. It is suggested to limit the length to 1 sentence. For instance, when the payment is timed out, the information in the field will be “No money implication- transaction declined”. In cases where money was deducted the response will be “Any amount deducted will be refunded within 5-7 working days”.

## 3.12. perception (Internal)

This field offers an overview of the error, providing insight into how common the issue is and how Razorpay handles such situations. The content of the field is intended for the admin and merchant dashboards.  
**Content and Formatting**: This field helps manage merchant perception by providing context on the error. For instance, when an UPI collect request expires, the information in the field will be: " 30% of payment failures on UPI are due to customers not completing the payments within the stipulated time. While Razorpay ensures that payment requests are raised instantly, customers might take more time to finish the payment."

## 3.13. rzp\_actionable (Internal)

This field indicates whether Razorpay needs to take action by triggering a templatized response. The possible values are "No Action" or "CreateAutoResponse". This field is for internal use only and is not displayed anywhere.

## 3.14. next\_step (Internal)

This field outlines the recommended course of action for the merchant to resolve the error or mitigate its impact. Wherever applicable, if a merchant can instruct their customers to take a course of action, then the same can be part of the information in ‘next\_step’.  
**Content and Formatting**: The field is displayed in the dashboard and is intended to guide merchants through steps to address the error and ensure successful transactions. For example, in case of a payment timeout, the next steps will be ‘Please request your customer to pay within the specified time limits for the payment.’

# 4\. Exhaustive list of existing error codes

An exhaustive list of all error codes can be found [here](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1kZR2WOFCMlcwa6PILuVnyBMhnAnxXsOD4j_BmnFGujQ/edit?usp=sharing). The contents of the doc will be refreshed every month.

# **5\. When to design a new error response?**

Now that the basics have been covered let's focus on the key considerations when designing a new error response. The following sections provide a step-by-step guide to help you determine if an existing error message already addresses the use case you're working on. If a relevant error message is available, reuse it; otherwise, create a new one. We rigorously review the reasons for existing errors to prevent new and duplicate ones from being created. In most scenarios, given the exhaustive list of error reasons we already have, there is no good logic to create a new one. You truly have to encounter an exceptional scenario to create a new error reason so it's expected that you are thorough about it.  
Once the error message is created, it should be reviewed by both an engineering and product approver. Ensure there are no duplications, all fields are correctly mapped, and then submit it for approval to the appropriate council—either the API Council or the Payments API Council as per[API council \- Way of working](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vJK10_Ja6apSzJ2lwJ6OqATe3NhbHwbd9oOIiFJgs9o/edit?tab=t.0#heading=h.gjdgxs).

## 5.1. Razorpay side changes

A new error message will be necessitated when Razorpay introduces code changes with new error codes. For instance, a generic BAD\_REQUEST\_VALIDATION\_FAILED is broken down into specific errors like BAD\_REQUEST\_AMOUNT\_VALIDATION\_FAILED, BAD\_REQUEST\_CURRENCY\_NOT\_SUPPORTED. The following steps have to be followed to check if the error is existing in the system

* Filter the ‘public\_error\_code’ column in the EMM doc to check if the new error is categorized as ‘SERVER\_ERROR’ or ‘BAD\_REQUEST\_ERROR’ within the [Error Mapping Module](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1kZR2WOFCMlcwa6PILuVnyBMhnAnxXsOD4j_BmnFGujQ/edit?usp=sharing) doc  
* Identify the ‘source’, ‘step’ and ‘reason’ for the new error and evaluate if there are error messages that can be reused  
* If the error message can be reused, map the new internal error code to the existing error message, else create a new one

## 5.2. Gateway error code mapping updates

When a gateway introduces a new error or modifies an existing one, follow these steps:  
Gateway modifies existing gateway error code:

* Obtain the gateway error code (e.g., 'B1').  
* Check if the gateway error code is available in the ‘method’, ‘gateway\_action’ or ‘gateway’  tab of the doc [here](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1EA9nS6fJLJrX3yyt18IndqWJTZI4P4np7P_iZ-ZpPvg/edit?usp=sharing) under column ‘gateway\_error\_code’  
* Extract the corresponding internal error code \- in the above example this will be ‘BAD\_REQUEST\_REGISTERED\_MOBILE\_NUMBER\_NOT\_FOUND’  
* Verify if the content for the internal error code is available and can be reused from the [Error Mapping Module](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1kZR2WOFCMlcwa6PILuVnyBMhnAnxXsOD4j_BmnFGujQ/edit?usp=sharing) doc

Gateway introduces a new error code:

* Find all unmapped gateway errors  
* Find equivalent Razorpay reason codes from the [Error Mapping Module](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1kZR2WOFCMlcwa6PILuVnyBMhnAnxXsOD4j_BmnFGujQ/edit?usp=sharing) doc  
* Map the new error to existing reason codes if feasible, else create new error codes

## 5.3. Designing a new error message

Let’s say you’re creating a new system that doesn’t currently exist, like the UPI Switch. In this case, the first step is to understand the detailed process flow. Additionally, it’s important to ensure that the information received from NPCI is communicated to the merchant in the right context.  
Example Scenario:  
Imagine a refund attempt in which NPCI sends an error message: "PAYER ACCOUNT HAS CHANGED (REMITTER)." This error indicates that the refund couldn’t be processed because the bank account linked to the UPI ID has changed. The target audience for this message is the merchant.  
Here’s how we can create a merchant-facing error response:

* Check Existing Error Responses:  
  The first step is to check if a similar error response already exists in the system as detailed in the above sections. In this case, there isn’t one, so we need to create a new error message.  
* Define Error Details  
  We’ll define the details for each field related to this error:  
* **Description**:

  An easier approach to create a description is to re-format the NPCI error to ‘Payment failed as payer account has changed’. However, the content misses key details such as:

* This is a refund, not a payment.  
* The issue occurred with the UPI payment method.  
* The payer’s account refers to the account linked to their UPI ID.  
* Next steps for resolving the issue are unclear.

  A merchant side developer perusing such a description will have a hard time debugging the issue. Instead, changing the description to "Refund was unsuccessful because the bank account linked to this UPI ID has changed. Please try using a different account" makes it clear and avoids the need for further debugging from the merchant's end.

* **Code**:

  Given that the response came from gateway one can be tempted to call this a ‘GATEWAY\_ERROR’. Since the issue originates from the payer's action, the appropriate code here would be a ‘BAD\_REQUEST\_ERROR’. This indicates a client-side error and tells the development team to check the information provided.

* **Source**:

  Even though the request is initiated by the business, the problem stems from the customer changing their bank account linked to their UPI ID. Therefore, the source should be set to "customer."

* **Step**:

  In the given scenario, the issue occurs during the payment credit process. The appropriate step here would be "payment\_credit\_response", an existing step that can be reused.

* **Reason**:

  The failure is likely due to a change in the payer's linked account. A reason code like ‘payer\_account\_changed’ could be used, but this might be confusing \- does it refer to a UPI ID (VPA) change or a bank account change? A more specific reason would be "vpa\_linked\_account\_changed," which clearly identifies the problem as the bank account linked to the UPI ID having changed.

* **Metadata**: Include relevant details such as the payment ID. Additionally, the error message from NPCI should be passed to the merchant to provide full context.

Leveraging NotebookLM to fast-track API design process  
Author:  Renju Balu  
Date: Nov 15, 2024  
The model in Notebooklm [here](https://notebooklm.google.com/notebook/97cf6c61-e039-4993-864d-4ab8d74b76f0?_gl=1*1fhqf1g*_ga*NDM0NDc2MTgwLjE3MzA1OTk4NTk.*_ga_W0LDH41ZCB*MTczMDY0MTIwNi4zLjAuMTczMDY0MTIwOS41Ny4wLjA.) has been trained with the API design guide and publicly available Razorpay sources. This can be used to clarify the design guide's expectations and even test out new API designs. The model is intended for quick learning purposes; always do peer reviews before finalizing the API request and responses.  
**Note:** The model currently uses Razorpay public documentation and [API Design Guide](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/edit?usp=sharing) as sources, and responses will be limited to these.

  }

[\[1\]](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#ftnt_ref1) Content-Type header is [frequently confused](http://www.java-allandsundry.com/2012/08/accept-header-vs-content-type-header.html) with the Accept header. The former is a means for the client to define the format in which it is sending a request to the server. The latter is a way for the client to tell the server what kind of response it expects.  
[\[2\]](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#ftnt_ref2) In spite of this, whenever possible, we avoid changing the order of existing attributes in API responses. Our clients cannot be trusted.

[\[a\]](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#cmnt_ref1)Need to add a section on async APIs design and philosophy. For list of banks for switch API particularly. I am trying to add these request and response apis: /v1/banks/initiate and :prefix/v1/banks/callback. Is initiate correct? or we skip it. Async APIs design guideline would help.

[\[b\]](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#cmnt_ref2)Async APIs are generally best managed either by event specific webhooks or by api specific callback URLs.

[\[c\]](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vufulBF4-LYNJCixZTKtiwy4UZcqO3zcE9-hNl0iwY4/mobilebasic#cmnt_ref3)URI for async api to fetch bank accounts /v1/banks/initiate is good or we just call it /v1/banks
